        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/19017841-don-quijote-i">review of another edition</a>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10326280-john-caviglia?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10326280-john-caviglia?shelf=spanish">spanish</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1800321124" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10234450502444795692">At start: <br/><br/>Have decided to re, or re-re, or re-re-re read the Quijote (depending on where in the text) for the first time sequentially, in the (more or less) original Spanish, beginning to end, a chapter a day. Wonderful!<br/><br/>At end (to which there is no end): <br/><br/>Did not make my chapter a day, so it took me a little over two years :) But it's a good book to have looking over your shoulder as you go about life. Somewhere long ago I came across the fact that Thomas Mann read it while crossing the Atlantic </span>
  <span id="freeText10234450502444795692" style="display:none">At start: <br /><br />Have decided to re, or re-re, or re-re-re read the Quijote (depending on where in the text) for the first time sequentially, in the (more or less) original Spanish, beginning to end, a chapter a day. Wonderful!<br /><br />At end (to which there is no end): <br /><br />Did not make my chapter a day, so it took me a little over two years :) But it's a good book to have looking over your shoulder as you go about life. Somewhere long ago I came across the fact that Thomas Mann read it while crossing the Atlantic on a steamship, commenting something to the effect that this text deserved to be enjoyed while surrounded by vastness. Maybe I'm misremembering, but what Mann might have said seems right to me anyway. Still my favorite book of all time. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10234450502444795692" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2001046321" />
    <a title="framptonhollis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59980397-framptonhollis"><img alt="framptonhollis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520809126p2/59980397.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2001046321?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="framptonhollis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="framptonhollis" href="/user/show/59980397-framptonhollis">framptonhollis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781406791723" href="/book/show/1382972.Don_Quixote_de_La_Mancha_Vol_1">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59980397-framptonhollis?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59980397-framptonhollis?shelf=satire">satire</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59980397-framptonhollis?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59980397-framptonhollis?shelf=epic">epic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2001046321" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11863268284908205878">The legendary "heroic" figure of Don Quixote is one of the most famous and funny characters in the history of literature. Iconic, mad, brave, and deranged, his image remains iconic, and so do his adventures. This first part of Cervantes' classic epic satire is somewhat lengthy in sections, as Cervantes occasionally repeats himself and bores. But after any tedious section, Cervantes' astonishing comedy awaits to blast its way through the next, hugely entertaining page. Both clever and juvenile, t</span>
  <span id="freeText11863268284908205878" style="display:none">The legendary "heroic" figure of Don Quixote is one of the most famous and funny characters in the history of literature. Iconic, mad, brave, and deranged, his image remains iconic, and so do his adventures. This first part of Cervantes' classic epic satire is somewhat lengthy in sections, as Cervantes occasionally repeats himself and bores. But after any tedious section, Cervantes' astonishing comedy awaits to blast its way through the next, hugely entertaining page. Both clever and juvenile, this novel is brilliantly funny; almost all types of humor are used: slapstick, satire, silly insults, witty dialogue, comedy of manners, comedy of errors, slyly black humor, etc.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11863268284908205878" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_83888565" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/83888565" />
    <a title="Lynn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/999852-lynn"><img alt="Lynn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1205794584p2/999852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/83888565?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lynn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lynn" href="/user/show/999852-lynn">Lynn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789681658977" href="/book/show/6332308-el-ingenioso-hidalgo-don-quijote-de-la-mancha-1">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer83888565" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2297680162112605399">This is my favorite book of all time. I read the complete novel (both parts) in college for a Spanish class. I've read it 4 times...the complete version in English and Spanish, and the abridged version in English and Spanish. I'm getting the itch to read it again. I know it's not for most people, but after having a professor who was so knowledgeable about the book, it made me really appreciate the twists and turns, plot and character development, etc.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('si5HMD0FgiMR/2kM2qoPSKmsyK9hZ/9L0JLFnsqK2I5+w2Khbc17DFgmfnbeJky48uN6BDzeFWXq3HgeDCayUA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Id8EYjs+8jmIdJ8iFfhLadMKBozBDACxPBWjuAsxf0ntMiHza/YLFsGtiFgRdAiZiEW0J5y16p8GWx44zZ0Vlw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

Es la obra literaria más influyente no solo de la Era de Oro de la Literatura Española, pero también de toda literatura en la lengua española. El Quijote es una obra fundadora de la Literatura Occidental, siendo parte del Canon Occidental, siendo considerada la novela moderna, además de ser la más leída después de la Biblia. Es la primera obra genuinamente desmitificadora de la tradición caballeresca y cortés por su tratamiento burlesco. Representa la primera novela moderna y la primera novela polifónica; como tal, ejerció un enorme influjo en toda la narrativa europea.\n\nEl título de esta fue El Ingenioso caballero don Quijote de la Mancha y consta de 74 capítulos. En el prólogo, Cervantes se defiende irónicamente de las acusaciones del lopista Avellaneda y se lamenta de la dificultad del arte de novelar: la fantasía se vuelve tan insaciable como un perro hambriento. En la novela se juega con diversos planos de la realidad al incluir, dentro de ella, la edición de la primera parte del Quijote y, posteriormente, la de la apócrifa Segunda parte, que los personajes han leído. Cervantes se defiende de las inverosimilitudes que se han encontrado en la primera parte, como la misteriosa reaparición del rucio de Sancho después de ser robado por Ginés de Pasamonte y el destino de los dineros encontrados en una maleta de Sierra Morena, etc.\n\nAsí pues, en esta segunda entrega don Quijote y Sancho son conscientes del éxito editorial de la primera parte de sus aventuras y ya son célebres. De hecho, algunos de los personajes que aparecerán en lo sucesivo han leído el libro y los reconocen. Es más, en un alarde de clarividencia, tanto Cervantes como el propio don Quijote manifiestan que la novela pasará a convertirse en un clásico de la literatura y que la figura del hidalgo se verá a lo largo de los siglos como símbolo de La Mancha.\n\nLa obra empieza con el renovado propósito de don Quijote de volver a las andadas y sus preparativos para ello, no sin la fiera resistencia de su sobrina y el ama. El cura y el barbero tienen que confesar la locura de don Quijote y urden, junto al bachiller Sansón Carrasco, un nuevo plan que les permita recluir a don Quijote por un largo tiempo en su aldea. Por su parte, don Quijote renueva los ofrecimientos a Sancho prometiéndole la ansiada ínsula a cambio de su compañía. Sancho reacciona obsesionándose con la idea de ser gobernador y cambiar de estatus social, lo que provoca la burla de su esposa Teresa Panza. Con conocimiento de sus convecinos don Quijote y Sancho inician su tercera salida.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"14928617552629572449\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return In the company of his faithful squire, Sancho Panza, his exploits blossom in all sorts of wonderful ways. While Quixote\'s fancy often leads him astray—he tilts at windmills, imagining them to be giants—Sancho acquires cunning and a certain sagacity. Sane madman and wise fool, they roam the world together, and together they have haunted readers\' imaginations for nearly four hundred years.\n\nWith its experimental form and literary playfulness, Don Quixote has been generally recognized as the first modern novel. The book has been enormously influential on a host of writers, from Fielding and Sterne to Flaubert, Dickens, Melville, and Faulkner, who reread it once a year, &quot;just as some people read the       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/4037220.Miguel_de_Cervantes_Saavedra">About Miguel de Cervantes Saavedra</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/4037220.Miguel_de_Cervantes_Saavedra"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1276109217p3/4037220.jpg);'></div>

<a href="/author/show/4037220.Miguel_de_Cervantes_Saavedra">Miguel de Cervantes Saavedra

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6483256653064855683">Miguel de Cervantes Saavedra was a Spanish novelist, poet, and playwright. His novel <i>Don Quixote</i> is often considered his magnum opus, as well as the first modern novel.<br/>It is assumed that Miguel de Cervantes was born in Alcalá de Henares. His father was Rodrigo de Cervantes, a surgeon of cordoban descent. Little is known of his mother Leonor de Cortinas, except that she was a native of Arganda del </span>
  <span id="freeText6483256653064855683" style="display:none">Miguel de Cervantes Saavedra was a Spanish novelist, poet, and playwright. His novel <i>Don Quixote</i> is often considered his magnum opus, as well as the first modern novel.<br />It is assumed that Miguel de Cervantes was born in Alcalá de Henares. His father was Rodrigo de Cervantes, a surgeon of cordoban descent. Little is known of his mother Leonor de Cortinas, except that she was a native of Arganda del Rey.<br />In 1569, Cervantes moved to Italy, where he served as a valet to Giulio Acquaviva, a wealthy priest who was elevated to cardinal the next year. By then, Cervantes had enlisted as a soldier in a Spanish Navy infantry regiment and continued his military life until 1575, when he was captured by Algerian corsairs. He was then released on ransom from his captors by his parents and the Trinitarians, a Catholic religious order. He subsequently returned to his family in Madrid.<br />In Esquivias (Province of Toledo), on 12 December 1584, he married the much younger Catalina de Salazar y Palacios (Toledo, Esquivias –, 31 October 1626), daughter of Fernando de Salazar y Vozmediano and Catalina de Palacios. Her uncle Alonso de Quesada y Salazar is said to have inspired the character of Don Quixote. During the next 20 years Cervantes led a nomadic existence, working as a purchasing agent for the Spanish Armada and as a tax collector. He suffered a bankruptcy and was imprisoned at least twice (1597 and 1602) for irregularities in his accounts. Between 1596 and 1600, he lived primarily in Seville. In 1606, Cervantes settled in Madrid, where he remained for the rest of his life.<br />Cervantes died in Madrid on April 23, 1616.<br /><i>-Copied from Wikipedia</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="6483256653064855683" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1382974.Don_Quixote_de_La_Mancha_II"><img alt="Don Quixote de La Mancha II (Don Quijote de la Mancha, #2)" style="height: 75px;" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1347607129l/1382974._SY75_.jpg" />
</a>


<script>
//<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_1382974'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1382974.Don_Quixote_de_La_Mancha_II?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">Don Quixote de La Mancha II (Don Quijote de la Mancha, #2)<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/4037220.Miguel_de_Cervantes_Saavedra?origin=series_works\">Miguel de Cervantes Saavedra<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.19 avg rating &mdash; 3,602 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 1615\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer7156279740664159692\">Publicada su segunda parte con el título de El ingenioso caballero Don Quijote de la Mancha en 1615, diez años después de la primera parte, durante los últimos años de vida del autor, en parte como respuesta a la falsa segunda parte del Quijote de Al<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText7156279740664159692\" style=\"display:none\">Publicada su segunda parte con el título de El ingenioso caballero Don Quijote de la Mancha en 1615, diez años después de la primera parte, durante los últimos años de vida del autor, en parte como respuesta a la falsa segunda parte del Quijote de Alonso Fernández de Avellaneda en 1614, acerca la cual Cervantes escribió irónicamente en el Prólogo. Es la obra literaria más influyente no solo de la Era de Oro de la Literatura Española, pero también de toda literatura en la lengua española. El Quijote es una obra fundadora de la Literatura Occidental, siendo parte del Canon Occidental, siendo considerada la novela moderna, además de ser la más leída después de la Biblia. Es la primera obra genuinamente desmitificadora de la tradición caballeresca y cortés por su tratamiento burlesco. Representa la primera novela moderna y la primera novela polifónica; como tal, ejerció un enorme influjo en toda la narrativa europea.\n\nEl título de esta fue El Ingenioso caballero don Quijote de la Mancha y consta de 74 capítulos. En el prólogo, Cervantes se defiende irónicamente de las acusaciones del lopista Avellaneda y se lamenta de la dificultad del arte de novelar: la fantasía se vuelve tan insaciable como un perro hambriento. En la novela se juega con diversos planos de la realidad al incluir, dentro de ella, la edición de la primera parte del Quijote y, posteriormente, la de la apócrifa Segunda parte, que los personajes han leído. Cervantes se defiende de las inverosimilitudes que se han encontrado en la primera parte, como la misteriosa reaparición del rucio de Sancho después de ser robado por Ginés de Pasamonte y el destino de los dineros encontrados en una maleta de Sierra Morena, etc.\n\nAsí pues, en esta segunda entrega don Quijote y Sancho son conscientes del éxito editorial de la primera parte de sus aventuras y ya son célebres. De hecho, algunos de los personajes que aparecerán en lo sucesivo han leído el libro y los reconocen. Es más, en un alarde de clarividencia, tanto Cervantes como el propio don Quijote manifiestan que la novela pasará a convertirse en un clásico de la literatura y que la figura del hidalgo se verá a lo largo de los siglos como símbolo de La Mancha.\n\nLa obra empieza con el renovado propósito de don Quijote de volver a las andadas y sus preparativos para ello, no sin la fiera resistencia de su sobrina y el ama. El cura y el barbero tienen que confesar la locura de don Quijote y urden, junto al bachiller Sansón Carrasco, un nuevo plan que les permita recluir a don Quijote por un largo tiempo en su aldea. Por su parte, don Quijote renueva los ofrecimientos a Sancho prometiéndole la ansiada ínsula a cambio de su compañía. Sancho reacciona obsesionándose con la idea de ser gobernador y cambiar de estatus social, lo que provoca la burla de su esposa Teresa Panza. Con conocimiento de sus convecinos don Quijote y Sancho inician su tercera salida.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"7156279740664159692\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n    <\/div>\n\n      <div class=\'wtrButtonContainer wtrSignedOut\' id=\'25_book_1382974\'>\n<div class=\'wtrUp wtrLeft\'>\n<form action=\"/shelf/add_to_shelf\"
